Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Accuracy   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Accuracy

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Accuracy is a leaf node.

Description

The difference between the approximate solutions obtained using a numerical model and the exact solution of the governing equations. The degree of conformity of a measure to a standard or true value

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Aggradation   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Aggradation

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Aggradation is a leaf node.

Description

The geologic process by which stream beds, floodplains, and the bottoms of other water bodies are raised in elevation by the deposition of material eroded and transported from other areas. It is the opposite of degradation.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Algorithm is a leaf node.

Description

A procedure for solving a mathematical problem in a finite number of steps that frequently involves repetition of an operation. A step by step procedure for solving a problem or accomplishing an end. A set of numerical steps or routines to obtain a numerical output from a numerical input.

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Alluvial_Fan   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Alluvial_Fan

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Alluvial_Fan is a leaf node.

Description

A conical, or fan, shaped deposit at the base of a mountain range where the mountain stream encounters the lesser slope of the valley floor. The deposits are generally coarse and alluvial fans most often occur in arid and semi-arid regions where streamflow is ephemeral and vegetation cover is sparse.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Alluvial_Stream   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Alluvial_Stream

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Alluvial_Stream is a leaf node.

Description

A stream whose channel boundary is composed of
appreciable quantities of the sediments transported by
the flow, and which generally changes its bed forms as
the rate of flow changes.

Implementation:

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Alluvium   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Alluvium

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Alluvium is a leaf node.

Description

A general term for all detrital deposits resulting directly or indirectly from the sediment transported by (modern) streams; thus including the sediments laid down in river beds, floodplains, lakes, fans, and estuaries.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Anomaly   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Anomaly

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Anomaly is a leaf node.

Description

(1) A departure from the expected or normal. (2) A geological feature, esp. in the subsurface, distinguished by geological, geophysical, or geochemical means, which is different from the general surroundings and is often of potential value.

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Armoring   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Armoring

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Armoring is a leaf node.

Description

The process of progressive coarsening of the bed layer by removal of fine particles until it becomes resistant to scour. The coarse layer that remains on the surface is termed the "armor layer." Armoring is a temporary condition; higher flows may destroy an armor layer and it may reform as flows decrease. Or, simply, the formation of a resistant layer of relatively large particles resulting from removal of finer particles by erosion.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

skos:Concept ;

dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/Portals/76/Publications/EngineerManuals/EM_1110-2-1416.pdf#page=132" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-2-1416.yaml#term[Armoring]" ;

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Bed_Forms   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Bed_Forms

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Bed_Forms is a leaf node.

Description

Irregularities found on the bottom (bed) of a stream that are related to flow characteristics. They are given names such as "dunes," "ripples," and "antidunes." They are related to the transport of sediment and interact with the flow because they change the roughness of the stream bed. An analog to stream bed forms are desert sand dunes (although the physical mechanisms for their creation and movement may be different).

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-2-1416:Bed_Forms a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Bed Forms" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/Portals/76/Publications/EngineerManuals/EM_1110-2-1416.pdf#page=133" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-2-1416.yaml#term[Bed Forms]" ;
skos:definition "Irregularities found on the bottom (bed) of a stream that are related to flow characteristics. Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Bed_Load   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Bed_Load

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Bed_Load is a leaf node.

Description

Material moving on or near the stream bed by rolling, sliding, and sometimes making brief excursions into the flow a few diameters above the bed, i.e. jumping. The term "saltation" is sometimes used in place of "jumping." Bed load is bed material that moves in continuous contact with the bed; contrast with "suspended load."

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Bed_Material

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Bed_Material is a leaf node.

Description

The sediment mixture of which the moving bed is composed. In alluvial streams, bed material particles are likely to be moved at any moment or during some future flow condition.

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Boundary_Roughness is a leaf node.

Description

The roughness of the bed and banks of a stream or river. The greater the roughness, the greater the frictional resistance to flows; and, hence, the greater the water surface elevation for any given discharge.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Braided_Channel is a leaf node.

Description

A stream that is characterized by random interconnected channels divided by islands or bars. Bars which divide the stream into separate channels at low flows are often submerged at high flow.

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Channel_Stabilization   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Channel_Stabilization

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Channel_Stabilization is a leaf node.

Description

A stable channel is neither progressively aggrading nor degrading, or changing its cross-sectional area through time. It could aggrade or degrade slightly, but over the period of a year, the channel would remain similar in shape and dimensions and position to previous times. Unstable channels are depositing or eroding in response to some exterior conditions. Stabilization techniques consist of bank protection and other measures that work to transform an unstable channel into a stable one.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Conveyance   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Conveyance

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Conveyance is a leaf node.

Description

A measure of the flow carrying capacity of a channel section. Flow is directly proportional to conveyance for steady flow. From Manning's equation, the proportionality factor is the square root of the energy slope.

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Degradation   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Degradation

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Degradation is a leaf node.

Description

The geologic process by which stream beds, floodplains, and the bottoms of other water bodies are lowered in elevation by the removal of material from the boundary. It is the opposite of aggradation.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Dimensionless_Number   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Dimensionless_Number

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Dimensionless_Number is a leaf node.

Description

A physically meaningful ratio of parameters that is dimensionless. These dimensionless ratios are useful in determining scaling laws since a particular dimensionless number must be the same in both model and prototype to achieve similarity. Examples are the common force ratios, such as the Froude and Reynolds
numbers.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Dominant_Discharge   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Dominant_Discharge

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Dominant_Discharge is a leaf node.

Description

A particular magnitude of flow which is sometimes referred to as the "channel forming" discharge. Empirical relations have been developed between "equilibrium" stream width, depth, and slope and the dominant discharge. It has been variously defined as the bank full flow, mean annual discharge, etc.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Dunes   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Dunes

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Dunes is a leaf node.

Description

Bed forms with triangular profile that advance downstream due to net deposition of particles on the steep downstream slope. Dunes move downstream at velocities that are small relative to the streamflow velocity.

Implementation:

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Flow_Duration_Curve   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Flow_Duration_Curve

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Flow_Duration_Curve is a leaf node.

Description

A measure of the range and variability of a stream's flow. The flow duration curve represents the percent of time during which specified flow rates are exceeded at a given location. This is usually presented as a graph of flow rate (discharge) versus percent of time that flows are greater than, or equal to, that flow.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Froude_Number   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Froude_Number

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Froude_Number is a leaf node.

Description

U/(gL) (U = velocity, g = gravity, L = length). A dimensionless number expressing the ratio between the influences of inertia and gravity in a fluid. The Froude number is important wherever the gravity effect is dominating, such as with water waves, flow in open channels, sedimentation in lakes and reservoirs, salt-water intrusions, and the mixing of air masses of different densities.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-2-1416:Froude_Number a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Froude Number" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/Portals/76/Publications/EngineerManuals/EM_1110-2-1416.pdf#page=136" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-2-1416.yaml#term[Froude Number]" ;
skos:definition "U/(gL) (U = velocity, g = gravity, L = length). A dimensionless number expressing the ratio between the influences of inertia and gravity in a fluid. The Froude number is important wherever the gravity effect is dominating, such as with water waves, flow in open channels, sedimentation in lakes and reservoirs, salt-water intrusions, and the mixing of air masses of different densities." ;
skos:inScheme EM-1110-2-1416: ;

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Geologic_Control   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Geologic_Control

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Geologic_Control is a leaf node.

Description

A local rock formation or clay layer that limits (within the engineering time frame) the vertical and/or lateral movement of a stream at a particular point. Note that artificial controls such as drop structures also exist.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Implicit_Scheme   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Implicit_Scheme

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Implicit_Scheme is a leaf node.

Description

Scheme in which the governing equations of a numerical model are arranged to obtain solutions for the dependent variables simultaneously at all grid points corresponding to any one time. The computed values depend not only on known values at a previous time but also on the other unknown neighboring values at the surrounding grid points at the time being calculated.
(Compare with EXPLICIT SCHEME).

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-2-1416:Implicit_Scheme a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Implicit Scheme" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/Portals/76/Publications/EngineerManuals/EM_1110-2-1416.pdf#page=136" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-2-1416.yaml#term[Implicit Scheme]" ;
skos:definition """Scheme in which the governing equations of a numerical model are arranged to obtain solutions for the dependent variables simultaneously at all grid points corresponding to any one time. The computed values depend not only on known values at a previous time but also on the other unknown neighboring values at the surrounding grid points at the time being calculated.
(Compare with EXPLICIT SCHEME).""" ;

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Initial_Conditions   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Initial_Conditions

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Initial_Conditions is a leaf node.

Description

The values of water levels, velocities, concentrations, etc., that are specified everywhere in the grid or mesh at the beginning of a model run. For iterative solutions, the initial conditions represent the first estimate of the variables the model is trying to compute.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Manning%27s_n-Value   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Manning%27s_n-Value

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Manning%27s_n-Value is a leaf node.

Description

n is a coefficient of boundary roughness. n accounts for energy loss due to the friction between the bed and the water. In fluvial hydraulics (movable boundary hydraulics), the Manning's n value usually includes the effects of other losses, such as grain roughness of the movable bed, form roughness of the movable bed, bank irregularities, vegetation, bend losses, and junction losses. Contraction and expansion losses are not included in Manning's n, and are typically accounted for separately.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-2-1416:Manning%27s_n-Value a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Manning's n-Value" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/Portals/76/Publications/EngineerManuals/EM_1110-2-1416.pdf#page=137" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-2-1416.yaml#term[Manning's n-Value]" ;
skos:definition "n is a coefficient of boundary roughness. n accounts for energy loss due to the friction between the bed and the water. In fluvial hydraulics (movable boundary hydraulics), the Manning's n value usually includes the effects of other losses, such as grain roughness of the movable bed, form roughness of the movable bed, bank irregularities, vegetation, bend losses, and junction losses. Contraction and expansion losses are not included in Manning's n, and are typically accounted for separately." ;

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Meandering_Stream   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Meandering_Stream

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Meandering_Stream is a leaf node.

Description

An alluvial stream characterized in planform by a series of pronounced alternating bends. The shape and existence of the bends in a meandering stream are a result of alluvial processes and not determined by the nature of the terrain (geology) through which the stream flows.

Implementation:

Description

A representation of a physical process or thing that can be used to predict the process's or thing's behavior or state. Examples: A conceptual model: If I throw a rock harder, it will go faster. A mathematical model: F = ma A hydraulic model: Columbia River physical model.

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Numerical_Model   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Numerical_Model

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Numerical_Model is a leaf node.

Description

A numerical model is the representation of a mathematical model as a sequence of instructions (program) for a computer. Given appropriate data, the
execution of this sequence of instructions yields an
approximate solution to the set of equations that comprise the mathematical model.

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Phasing is a leaf node.

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Reynolds_Number   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Reynolds_Number

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Reynolds_Number is a leaf node.

Description

(UL)/ - Dimensionless ratio of inertial force to viscous force; the length may represent grain size, depth of flow, or pipe diameter, resulting in different Reynolds Numbers for different purposes. The critical Reynolds Number describes the onset of turbulence. The Reynolds number is defined as velocity multiplied by length divided by kinematic viscosity. It is usually involved wherever viscosity is important, such as in slow movement of fluid in small passages or around small objects.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-2-1416:Reynolds_Number a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Reynolds Number" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/Portals/76/Publications/EngineerManuals/EM_1110-2-1416.pdf#page=138" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-2-1416.yaml#term[Reynolds Number]" ;
skos:definition "(UL)/ - Dimensionless ratio of inertial force to viscous force; the length may represent grain size, depth of flow, or pipe diameter, resulting in different Reynolds Numbers for different purposes. The critical Reynolds Number describes the onset of turbulence. The Reynolds number is defined as velocity multiplied by length divided by kinematic viscosity. It is usually involved wherever viscosity is important, such as in slow movement of fluid in small passages or around small objects." ;
skos:inScheme EM-1110-2-1416: ;
skos:prefLabel "Reynolds Number" .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Ripple   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Ripple

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Ripple is a leaf node.

Description

Small triangular-shaped bed forms that are similar to dunes but have much smaller heights and lengths of 0.3 m or less. They develop when the Froude number is less than approximately 0.3.

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Scale_Effect   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Scale_Effect

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Scale_Effect is a leaf node.

Description

Consequence of nonsimilarity between model and prototype resulting from the fact that not all pertinent dimensionless numbers are the same in model and prototype. In a "perfect" model, all pertinent dimensionless numbers are the same in model and prototype. In a "real" model, economics dictates the use of certain materials, e.g., water as a fluid. This means that fluid density and viscosity are not correctly scaled down from prototype to model and, as a consequence, some dimensionless numbers are not the same in model and prototype, resulting in scale effect.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-2-1416:Scale_Effect a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Scale Effect" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/Portals/76/Publications/EngineerManuals/EM_1110-2-1416.pdf#page=139" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-2-1416.yaml#term[Scale Effect]" ;
skos:definition "Consequence of nonsimilarity between model and prototype resulting from the fact that not all pertinent dimensionless numbers are the same in model and prototype. In a \"perfect\" model, all pertinent dimensionless numbers are the same in model and prototype. In a \"real\" model, economics dictates the use of certain materials, e.g., water as a fluid. This means that fluid density and viscosity are not correctly scaled down from prototype to model and, as a consequence, some dimensionless numbers are not the same in model and prototype, resulting in scale effect." ;
skos:inScheme EM-1110-2-1416: ;
skos:prefLabel "Scale Effect" .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Sediment_Transport_Function   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Sediment_Transport_Function

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Sediment_Transport_Function is a leaf node.

Description

A formula or algorithm for calculating sediment transport rate given the hydraulics and bed material at a cross section. Most sediment transport functions compute the bed material load capacity. The actual transport may be less than the computed capacity due to armoring, geologic controls, etc. or greater due to fine material (wash load) that originates upstream rather than from the bed.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Sediment_Yield   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Sediment_Yield

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Sediment_Yield is a leaf node.

Description

The total sediment outflow from a drainage basin in a specific period of time. It includes bed load as well as suspended load, and is usually expressed in terms of mass or volume per unit of time.

Implementation:

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Sedimentation   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Sedimentation

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Sedimentation is a leaf node.

Description

Consists of five fundamental processes: (1) weathering, (2) erosion, (3) transportation, (4) deposition, and (5) diagenesis, or consolidation into rock. Also refers to the gravitational settling of suspended particles that are heavier than water.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Shear_Force   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Shear_Force

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Shear_Force is a leaf node.

Description

The shear force is the shear developed on the wetted area of the channel and it acts in the direction of flow. This force per unit wetted area is called the shear stress.

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Sinuosity

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Sinuosity is a leaf node.

Description

A measure of meander "intensity." Computed as the ratio of the length of a stream measured along its thalweg (or centerline) to the length of the valley through which the stream flows.

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Stability is a leaf node.

Description

The ability of a scheme to control the propagation or growth of small perturbations introduced in the calculations. A scheme is unstable if it allows the growth of error to eventually obliterate the true solution.

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Transport_Capacity   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Transport_Capacity

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Transport_Capacity is a leaf node.

Description

The ability of a stream to transport a given volume or weight of sediment material of a specific size per time for a given flow condition. The units of transport capacity are usually given in tons per day of sediment passing a given cross section for a given flow. Transport capacity for each sediment grain size is the transport potential for that size multiplied by the actual fraction of that size class present in the bed material.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-2-1416:Transport_Capacity a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Transport Capacity" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/Portals/76/Publications/EngineerManuals/EM_1110-2-1416.pdf#page=141" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-2-1416.yaml#term[Transport Capacity]" ;

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Trap_Efficiency   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Trap_Efficiency

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Trap_Efficiency is a leaf node.

Description

Proportion of sediment inflow to a stream reach (or reservoir) that is retained within that reach (or reservoir). Computed as inflowing sediment volume minus outflowing sediment volume divided by inflowing sediment volume. Positive values indicate aggradation; negative values, degradation.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .

pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-2-1416.yaml#term[Trap Efficiency]" ;

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Truncation_Error   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Truncation_Error

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Truncation_Error is a leaf node.

Description

The error introduced by replacing the derivative terms of a differential equation by finite differences using a Taylor series and then truncating after a certain number
of terms.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .

Concept: EM-1110-2-1416:Validation   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-2-1416:Validation

NOTE EM-1110-2-1416:Validation is a leaf node.

Description

Comparison of model results with a set of prototype data that were not used for verification. Comparison includes: (1) sing a data set very similar to the verification data to determine the validity of the model under conditions for which it was designed; (2) sing a data set quite different from the verification data to determine the validity of the model under conditions for which it was not designed but could possibly be used; and (3) using post-construction prototype data to determine the validity of the predictions based on model results.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-2-1416: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-2-1416#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
